PlayerProfile\r\nzero or more role assignments\r\nzero or more secure sessions\r\n```\r\n\r\nA person must not need separate logins for Player, Captain, and Creator capabilities.\r\n\r\n## 9.2 Every to:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nPLAYER\r\nCAPTAIN\r\nCREATOR\r\nMODERATOR\r\nADMINISTRATOR\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe exact representation may follow repository conventions, but role checks must resolve from the canonical account.\r\n\r\nDo not derive authorization from visible display names, email addresses, or legacy username strings.\r\n\r\n## 9.4 Login identity is private\r\n\r\nThe following must never become public profile identity automatically:\r\n\r\n* email;\r\n* normalized email;\r\n* password metadata;\r\n* session IDs;\r\n* reset tokens;\r\n* verification tokens;\r\n* IP information;\r\n* user-agent fingerprints;\r\n* provider IDs;\r\n* security events.\r\n\r\n## 9.5 Display name is independent\r\n\r\nEvery profile must have a visible `displayName`.\r\n\r\nThe display name:\r\n\r\n* is not the email;\r\n* need not be globally unique;\r\n* may be changed through governed profile behavior;\r\n* is the default person-facing label;\r\n* is stored separately from authentication identity.\r\n\r\nPhase 1 does not need the final public handle system, but it must not misuse email as a visible fallback.\r\n\r\n## 9.6 Authoritative relations\r\n\r\nNew person-owned writes must use canonical account or profile relations.\r\n\r\nRaw string actor fields may remain temporarily for compatibility or historical snapshots, but must not remain the only source of truth for new writes.\r\n\r\n## 9.7 History preservation\r\n\r\nAccount creation, claiming, migration, role consolidation, and password recovery must not lose:\r\n\r\n* memberships;\r\n* invitations;\r\n* invitation events;\r\n* Player status;\r\n* join timestamps;\r\n* completion timestamps;\r\n* pinned or hidden states;\r\n* Captain sessions;\r\n* Creator ownership;\r\n* published-version attribution;\r\n* audit history.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 10. Mandatory Phase 1 Design Record\r\n\r\nBefore implementing schema changes, create:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nDevelopment_Docs/Project_Wayfarer_Phase_1_Design_Record.md\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe design record must freeze these decisions:\r\n\r\n1. canonical account model;\r\n2. guest identity model;\r\n3. account/profile cardinality;\r\n4. current `username` semantics;\r\n5. display-name semantics;\r\n6. email normalization;\r\n7. email verification;\r\n8. password credential ownership;\r\n9. password hashing policy;\r\n10. account-session architecture;\r\n11. CSRF policy;\r\n12. role assignment architecture;\r\n13. `GameMasterUser` migration strategy;\r\n14. `PlayerProfile` credential migration strategy;\r\n15. `PlayerIdentitySession` migration strategy;\r\n16. `GameMasterSession` migration strategy;\r\n17. duplicate identity resolution;\r\n18. guest claim into a new account;\r\n19. guest claim into an existing account;\r\n20. same-Voyage membership collision handling;\r\n21. raw actor-field migration;\r\n22. actor display snapshots;\r\n23. compatibility adapters;\r\n24. transactional email boundary;\r\n25. audit and security events;\r\n26. token storage and expiry;\r\n27. migration rollback or restore strategy;\r\n28. testing database isolation;\r\n29. later provider-integration seam;\r\n30. later profile and statistics seam.\r\n\r\nDo not begin parallel source implementation until these contracts are stable.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 11. Canonical Account Model\r\n\r\n## 11.1 Required concept\r\n\r\nIntroduce a canonical account model equivalent to:\r\n\r\n```ts\r\nUserAccount\r\n```\r\n\r\nRecommended conceptual fields:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nid\r\nstatus\r\nclaimedAt\r\ncreatedAt\r\nupdatedAt\r\nlastSeenAt\r\nlockedAt\r\nsuspendedAt\r\ndeletionRequestedAt\r\ndeletedAt\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe exact field list may be adapted to current conventions, but Phase 1 must support at least:\r\n\r\n* active claimed account;\r\n* unverified account;\r\n* guest or unclaimed identity;\r\n* locked or suspended state;\r\n* session ownership;\r\n* profile ownership;\r\n* role ownership;\r\n* security-event ownership.\r\n\r\n## 11.2 Guest strategy\r\n\r\nChoose and document one of these approaches:\r\n\r\n### Preferred option\r\n\r\nCreate a canonical `UserAccount` even for an invited guest:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nstatus = GUEST_UNCLAIMED\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe guest account:\r\n\r\n* owns one profile;\r\n* owns temporary sessions;\r\n* has no verified email;\r\n* has no password credential;\r\n* upgrades in place during claiming.\r\n\r\nThis avoids changing the personâ€™s canonical account ID during claiming.\r\n\r\n### Acceptable compatibility option\r\n\r\nAllow an unclaimed `PlayerProfile` without a `UserAccount`, retain a guest-specific session, and create or attach a `UserAccount` during claiming.\r\n\r\nThis is acceptable only if:\r\n\r\n* history migration is transactional;\r\n* guest sessions are revoked or converted safely;\r\n* duplicate claiming is idempotent;\r\n* no person-owned records are lost;\r\n* the design record explains why the preferred option was not practical.\r\n\r\nDo not create accountless canonical sessions.\r\n\r\n## 11.3 Account/profile relationship\r\n\r\nThe final claimed architecture must enforce:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nUserAccount 1:1 PlayerProfile\r\n```\r\n\r\nPossible implementation:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nPlayerProfile.accountId String? @unique\r\n```\r\n\r\nduring additive migration, later becoming required for claimed profiles.\r\n\r\nDo not destructively require the relation before existing data has been backfilled and reconciled.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 12. Player Profile Migration\r\n\r\n## 12.1 Existing profile preservation\r\n\r\nExisting `PlayerProfile.id` values should remain stable whenever practical.\r\n\r\nDo not recreate every profile with new IDs merely to make the schema aesthetically cleaner.\r\n\r\nPreserve:\r\n\r\n* display name;\r\n* status;\r\n* claimed timestamp;\r\n* created timestamp;\r\n* updated timestamp;\r\n* last seen;\r\n* memberships;\r\n* invitations;\r\n* Player sessions;\r\n* preference data.\r\n\r\n## 12.2 Existing username\r\n\r\nThe current `PlayerProfile.username` may have ambiguous semantics.\r\n\r\nIt may currently represent:\r\n\r\n* login username;\r\n* public username;\r\n* test fixture label;\r\n* intended future handle.\r\n\r\nDo not guess.\r\n\r\nInventory actual usage.\r\n\r\nThe design record must choose one transition:\r\n\r\n### Option A: legacy login alias\r\n\r\nPreserve current username in a compatibility login-alias structure.\r\n\r\nDo not expose it publicly automatically.\r\n\r\n### Option B: provisional public handle\r\n\r\nUse it as a public handle only when current behavior and product language clearly support that interpretation.\r\n\r\n### Option C: deprecated compatibility field\r\n\r\nRetain it temporarily, stop new writes, and migrate login behavior to verified email.\r\n\r\nNever silently convert an email-like username into a public handle.\r\n\r\n## 12.3 Existing password hash\r\n\r\nIf a `PlayerProfile` has a password hash:\r\n\r\n* migrate or associate it with the canonical account credential;\r\n* preserve the current hashing algorithm;\r\n* do not rehash without the plaintext password;\r\n* mark the algorithm/version when practical;\r\n* upgrade the hash after a successful future login if current security policy requires it.\r\n\r\nDo not log hashes.\r\n\r\nDo not copy a hash i…24 tokens truncated…r experience;\r\n4. enter Captain experience;\r\n5. enter Creator Studio;\r\n6. verify no second login;\r\n7. verify backend authorization.\r\n\r\n## E3: Forgotten password\r\n\r\n1. create active sessions on two devices;\r\n2. request reset;\r\n3. retrieve test reset link;\r\n4. set new password;\r\n5. verify old password fails;\r\n6. verify both old sessions are revoked;\r\n7. sign in with new password;\r\n8. verify security notice queued.\r\n\r\n## E4: Unknown reset email\r\n\r\n1. submit unregistered email;\r\n2. verify same visible response as registered email;\r\n3. verify no account details leak;\r\n4. verify no raw token appears in logs.\r\n\r\n## E5: Guest claim\r\n\r\n1. create invitation;\r\n2. open invitation unauthenticated;\r\n3. choose display name;\r\n4. enter Voyage as guest;\r\n5. claim with new email/password;\r\n6. verify account;\r\n7. return to Voyage;\r\n8. confirm membership and invitation unchanged.\r\n\r\n## E6: Guest merge into existing account\r\n\r\n1. sign out;\r\n2. create a second invitation guest;\r\n3. enter as guest;\r\n4. choose â€œuse existing accountâ€;\r\n5. authenticate;\r\n6. confirm merge;\r\n7. verify one Player profile remains;\r\n8. verify both Voyage histories remain;\r\n9. verify guest session is invalid.\r\n\r\n## E7: Session revocation\r\n\r\n1. create two sessions;\r\n2. revoke one;\r\n3. verify the other remains;\r\n4. sign out everywhere;\r\n5. verify both are invalid.\r\n\r\n## E8: Legacy compatibility\r\n\r\n1. sign in using an existing Player legacy identity;\r\n2. verify canonical session;\r\n3. sign in using an existing Captain/Creator legacy identity;\r\n4. verify canonical session and roles;\r\n5. verify no new legacy identity is created.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 41. Performance and Reliability Requirements\r\n\r\nPhase 1 is not a load-testing phase, but core behavior must be bounded.\r\n\r\nRequired targets:\r\n\r\n* ordinary sign-in service execution remains reasonable under current test environment;\r\n* token lookup uses indexed hashes;\r\n* email lookup uses indexed normalized email;\r\n* session lookup uses indexed token hash;\r\n* role resolution avoids unbounded query loops;\r\n* account/profile loading avoids repeated N+1 queries;\r\n* migration backfill works in bounded batches if dataset size requires it;\r\n* password reset request does not synchronously wait forever on external email;\r\n* repeated claim does not duplicate records;\r\n* failed email delivery does not roll back an already valid reset request into an inconsistent state;\r\n* no retry storm;\r\n* no unbounded session growth;\r\n* expired reset and verification tokens are cleanable.\r\n\r\nDocument query indexes added.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 42. Likely Files and Modules\r\n\r\nRevalidate actual paths before editing.\r\n\r\nPotential new modules:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nsrc/domain/accounts/\r\nsrc/domain/identity/\r\nsrc/domain/security/\r\nsrc/services/accounts/\r\nsrc/services/authentication/\r\nsrc/services/account-recovery/\r\nsrc/services/account-claim/\r\nsrc/services/account-sessions/\r\nsrc/services/roles/\r\nsrc/services/transactional-email/\r\nsrc/lib/auth/\r\nsrc/lib/security/\r\nsrc/lib/tokens/\r\nsrc/lib/email-normalization/\r\n```\r\n\r\nPotential routes:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nsrc/app/api/auth/register/route.ts\r\nsrc/app/api/auth/sign-in/route.ts\r\nsrc/app/api/auth/sign-out/route.ts\r\nsrc/app/api/auth/sign-out-all/route.ts\r\nsrc/app/api/auth/email/verify/route.ts\r\nsrc/app/api/auth/email/verification/resend/route.ts\r\nsrc/app/api/auth/password-reset/request/route.ts\r\nsrc/app/api/auth/password-reset/confirm/route.ts\r\nsrc/app/api/auth/sessions/route.ts\r\nsrc/app/api/auth/sessions/[sessionId]/revoke/route.ts\r\nsrc/app/api/auth/guest/claim/route.ts\r\nsrc/app/api/auth/guest/merge/route.ts\r\n```\r\n\r\nPotential pages:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nsrc/app/register/page.tsx\r\nsrc/app/sign-in/page.tsx\r\nsrc/app/forgot-password/page.tsx\r\nsrc/app/reset-password/page.tsx\r\nsrc/app/verify-email/page.tsx\r\nsrc/app/account/security/page.tsx\r\nsrc/app/account/claim/page.tsx\r\n```\r\n\r\nDo not create duplicate routes when equivalent current routes already exist.\r\n\r\nPrefer adapting existing surfaces.\r\n\r\nPotential schema changes:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nprisma/schema.prisma\r\nprisma/migrations/**/migration.sql\r\n```\r\n\r\nPotential tests:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nsrc/**/account*.test.ts\r\nsrc/**/auth*.test.ts\r\nsrc/**/recovery*.test.ts\r\nsrc/**/claim*.test.ts\r\ntests/e2e/account-lifecycle.spec.ts\r\ntests/e2e/guest-claim.spec.ts\r\ntests/e2e/role-unification.spec.ts\r\ntests/e2e/password-recovery.spec.ts\r\ntests/integration/wayfarer-migration.spec.ts\r\n```\r\n\r\nUse repository conventions.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 43. Implementation Order\r\n\r\nFollow this sequence.\r\n\r\n## Step 1: Repository and concurrent-work preflight\r\n\r\n* fetch origin;\r\n* record worktrees and status;\r\n* create isolated branch/worktree;\r\n* inspect current identity code;\r\n* inventory schema and routes;\r\n* identify concurrent overlaps.\r\n\r\n## Step 2: Design record\r\n\r\nFreeze:\r\n\r\n* canonical account;\r\n* guest strategy;\r\n* email;\r\n* credential;\r\n* session;\r\n* roles;\r\n* claiming;\r\n* migration;\r\n* actor relations;\r\n* compatibility.\r\n\r\nDo not parallelize shared implementation before this.\r\n\r\n## Step 3: Migration fixtures and reconciliation harness\r\n\r\nBefore changing production services:\r\n\r\n* create current-schema fixtures;\r\n* create migration test harness;\r\n* define expected counts;\r\n* define canonical database isolation proof.\r\n\r\n## Step 4: Additive canonical schema\r\n\r\nAdd:\r\n\r\n* UserAccount;\r\n* account/profile relation;\r\n* email;\r\n* verification token;\r\n* credential;\r\n* reset token;\r\n* canonical session;\r\n* security events;\r\n* canonical roles or updated role relation;\r\n* actor foreign-key seams.\r\n\r\nGenerate Prisma client.\r\n\r\nRun schema and migration tests.\r\n\r\n## Step 5: Backfill and compatibility mapping\r\n\r\nImplement:\r\n\r\n* PlayerProfile migration;\r\n* GameMasterUser migration;\r\n* credential migration;\r\n* session migration;\r\n* role migration;\r\n* explicit duplicate mapping;\r\n* raw actor backfill;\r\n* reconciliation report.\r\n\r\n## Step 6: Canonical services\r\n\r\nImplement:\r\n\r\n* account creation;\r\n* authentication;\r\n* authorization;\r\n* sessions;\r\n* verification;\r\n* password recovery;\r\n* guest claiming;\r\n* guest merge;\r\n* security events.\r\n\r\n## Step 7: Compatibility adapters\r\n\r\nUpdate:\r\n\r\n* existing Player authentication;\r\n* existing Game Master authentication;\r\n* Captain route guards;\r\n* Creator route guards;\r\n* Player session resolution;\r\n* role gateway;\r\n* invitation acceptance.\r\n\r\nAll must call canonical services.\r\n\r\n## Step 8: User-facing flows\r\n\r\nImplement or update:\r\n\r\n* registration;\r\n* sign-in;\r\n* forgot password;\r\n* reset password;\r\n* email verification;\r\n* guest claim;\r\n* account security and sessions.\r\n\r\n## Step 9: Actor cutover\r\n\r\nUpdate new writes to canonical actor relations.\r\n\r\nAdd fallback reads.\r\n\r\nTest Creator, Captain, invitation, reveal, and audit ownership.\r\n\r\n## Step 10: Focused tests\r\n\r\nRun service, migration, authorization, privacy, and UI tests.\r\n\r\nFix all task regressions before full validation.\r\n\r\n## Step 11: Isolated integration and E2E\r\n\r\nProve database identity.\r\n\r\nRun migration rehearsal.\r\n\r\nRun required E2E flows.\r\n\r\nVerify canonical database unchanged.\r\n\r\n## Step 12: Final validation\r\n\r\nRun one complete repository validation gate.\r\n\r\nRecord exact results.\r\n\r\n## Step 13: Compare with current main\r\n\r\nFetch latest `origin/main`.\r\n\r\nDo not merge.\r\n\r\nProduce:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nDevelopment_Docs/Project_Wayfarer_Phase_1_Integration_Manifest.md\r\n```\r\n\r\nDocument:\r\n\r\n* main movement since branch base;\r\n* changed files on both sides;\r\n* likely conflicts;\r\n* migration-order concerns;\r\n* recommended future integration order;\r\n* required post-merge validation.\r\n\r\n## Step 14: Commit and push\r\n\r\nCommit only Phase 1 files.\r\n\r\nPush the branch.\r\n\r\nStop for review.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 44. Suggested Commit Structure\r\n\r\nUse coherent commits such as:\r\n\r\n```text\r\ndocs(wayfarer): freeze phase 1 identity design\r\nfeat(wayfarer): add canonical account schema and migration\r\nfeat(auth): unify player captain and creator identity\r\nfeat(auth): add verification and password recovery\r\nfeat(auth): add guest account claiming and merge\r\ntest(wayfarer): validate identity lifecycle and migration\r\ndocs(wayfarer): record phase 1 validation and integration\r\n```\r\n\r\nThe exact number may differ.\r\n\r\nDo not create dozens of tiny noise commits.\r\n\r\nDo not squash away useful migration boundaries before review.\r\n\r\nDo not commit generated secrets, local databases, `.env` files, test inbox contents, or raw tokens.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 45. Validation Commands\r\n\r\nInspect `package.json` and use current repository-supported scripts.\r\n\r\nLikely commands include equivalents of:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nnpm run format:check\r\nnpm run lint\r\nnpm run typecheck\r\nnpm test\r\nnpm run build\r\nnpm run validate\r\n```\r\n\r\nAlso run the repositoryâ€™s correct Prisma commands, such as equivalents of:\r\n\r\n```text\r\nnpx prisma format\r\nnpx prisma validate\r\nnpx prisma generate\r\n```\r\n\r\nDo not invent unsupported scripts.\r\n\r\nRun focused tests first.\r\n\r\nRun the final full validation once after focused tests pass.\r\n\r\nDocument:\r\n\r\n* command;\r\n* environment;\r\n* database name;\r\n* exit code;\r\n* passed count;\r\n* failed count;\r\n* skipped count;\r\n* duration;\r\n* classification of any failure.\r\n\r\nA skipped test is not a pass.\r\n\r\nAn environmental failure is not a product pass.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 46. Required Documentation\r\n\r\n## 46.1 Design record\r\n\r\n```text\r\nDevelopment_Docs/Project_Wayfarer_Phase_1_Design_Record.md\r\n```\r\n\r\nMust contain:\r\n\r\n* architecture;\r\n* invariants;\r\n* schemas;\r\n* guest strategy;\r\n* role model;\r\n* username decision;\r\n* security decisions;\r\n* service boundaries;\r\n* actor inventory;\r\n* compatibility plan;\r\n* Phase 2 seams.\r\n\r\n## 46.2 Migration runbook\r\n\r\n```text\r\nDevelopment_Docs/Project_Wayfarer_Phase_1_Migration_Runbook.md\r\n```\r\n\r\nMust contain:\r\n\r\n* backup requirements;\r\n* isolated rehearsal;\r\n* migration sequence;\r\n* backfill;\r\n* reconciliation;\r\n* cutover;\r\n* rollback/restore;\r\n* legacy removal prerequisites;\r\n* unresolved identity handling.\r\n\r\n## 46.3 Test plan\r\n\r\n```text\r\nDevelopment_Docs/Project_Wayfarer_Phase_1_Test_Plan.md\r\n```\r\n\r\nMust map every acceptance criterion to tests.\r\n\r\n## 46.4 Validation record\r\n\r\n```text\r\nDevelopment_Docs/Project_Wayfarer_Phase_1_Validation_Record.md\r\n```\r\n\r\nMust contain actual commands and outcomes.\r\n\r\n## 46.5 Integration manifest\r\n\r\n```text\r\nDevelopment_Docs/Project_Wayfarer_Phase_1_Integration_Manifest.md\r\n```\r\n\r\nMust contain:\r\n\r\n* base SHA;\r\n* ending SHA;\r\n* latest main SHA;\r\n* branch file list;\r\n* latest-main file list;\r\n* conflicts;\r\n* schema ordering;\r\n* recommended merge steps;\r\n* post-merge validation.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 47. Exact Phase 1 Acceptance Criteria\r\n\r\nPhase 1 is complete only when every applicable criterion is satisfied.\r\n\r\n## 47.1 Canonical identity\r\n\r\n* `UserAccount` exists as the canonical authentication identity.\r\n* Every claimed account has one Player profile.\r\n* Captain and Creator privileges belong to the same canonical account.\r\n* A combined Player/Captain/Creator account signs in once.\r\n* Authorization uses canonical roles.\r\n* New code does not create independent Game Master identities.\r\n\r\n## 47.2 Display identity\r\n\r\n* Every profile has a visible display name.\r\n* Registration asks for display name.\r\n* Email is stored separately.\r\n* Email is not shown as the visible name.\r\n* Existing display names are preserved.\r\n* Legacy usernames have a documented migration meaning.\r\n\r\n## 47.3 Email\r\n\r\n* Primary normalized email is unique.\r\n* Verification token is hashed.\r\n* Verification token expires.\r\n* Verification token is single-use.\r\n* Verification is idempotent.\r\n* Resend is rate-limited.\r\n* No raw verification token is stored or logged.\r\n\r\n## 47.4 Registration\r\n\r\n* Registration creates account, profile, credential, email, role, and security event atomically.\r\n* Failed registration leaves no partial claimed account.\r\n* Password policy is enforced server-side.\r\n* Duplicate email race is handled safely.\r\n* New account can reach the Player experience according to verification policy.\r\n\r\n## 47.5 Password recovery\r\n\r\n* Forgot-password flow exists.\r\n* Unknown and known email requests produce indistinguishable visible responses.\r\n* Reset token is hashed, expiring, and single-use.\r\n* Old password fails after reset.\r\n* New password succeeds.\r\n* Existing sessions are revoked.\r\n* Other outstanding reset tokens are invalidated.\r\n* Password-changed notice is queued.\r\n* No secret is logged.\r\n\r\n## 47.6 Sessions\r\n\r\n* Canonical sessions belong to canonical accounts.\r\n* Current and other sessions can be listed safely.\r\n* One session can be revoked.\r\n* All sessions can be revoked.\r\n* Revocation takes effect immediately.\r\n* Password reset revokes sessions.\r\n* Guest sessions cannot access privileged roles.\r\n* Legacy sessions are migrated or intentionally revoked.\r\n\r\n## 47.7 Guest claiming\r\n\r\n* Invitation-first guest entry remains easy.\r\n* Guest identity is persistent.\r\n* Claim into new account preserves profile and membership.\r\n* Claim into existing account requires authentication.\r\n* Merge conflicts are deterministic.\r\n* No duplicate same-Voyage membership remains.\r\n* Guest session is revoked or converted.\r\n* Repeated claim is idempotent.\r\n* Merge is audited.\r\n\r\n## 47.8 Existing identity migration\r\n\r\n* Existing Player profiles are preserved.\r\n* Existing Player memberships are preserved.\r\n* Existing invitations are preserved.\r\n* Existing Game Master roles are preserved.\r\n* Existing Creator ownership is preserved.\r\n* Existing Captain ownership is preserved.\r\n* Existing credential hashes are not lost.\r\n* Ambiguous duplicates are not auto-merged.\r\n* Migration is rerunnable or safely resumable.\r\n* Reconciliation reports exact counts.\r\n\r\n## 47.9 Canonical actor IDs\r\n\r\n* New Tall Tale ownership writes canonical Creator account relation.\r\n* New session ownership writes canonical Captain account relation.\r\n* New invitations write canonical creator relation.\r\n* New audit/reveal actions write canonical actor relation where appropriate.\r\n* Historical actor snapshots remain readable.\r\n* Legacy raw strings are compatibility-only, not authorization sources.\r\n\r\n## 47.10 Compatibility\r\n\r\n* Existing Player flow works.\r\n* Existing Captain flow works.\r\n* Existing Creator Studio flow works.\r\n* Current invitation acceptance works.\r\n* Current publishing works.\r\n* Current Universal Language remains intact.\r\n* Current animation behavior is not regressed.\r\n* No unrelated subsystem is redesigned.\r\n\r\n## 47.11 Security\r\n\r\n* Passwords and hashes never enter logs.\r\n* Raw tokens never enter persistent storage.\r\n* State-changing cookie routes enforce CSRF.\r\n* Recovery is rate-limited.\r\n* Open redirects are rejected.\r\n* Locked and suspended accounts are enforced.\r\n* Public responses do not expose private identity data.\r\n\r\n## 47.12 Documentation and branch safety\r\n\r\n* Design record matches implementation.\r\n* Migration runbook is complete.\r\n* Test plan maps to tests.\r\n* Validation record contains actual evidence.\r\n* Integration manifest compares against current main.\r\n* Canonical checkout remained untouched.\r\n* Phase 1 branch is pushed.\r\n* Branch is not merged.\r\n* No unrelated files are committed.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# 48. Mandatory Final Report\r\n\r\nAt completion, provide a detailed final report containing:\r\n\r\n## Repository\r\n\r\n* repository;\r\n* canonical checkout path;\r\n* Phase 1 worktree path;\r\n* branch;\r\n* base commit;\r\n* ending commit;\r\n* latest origin/main;\r\n* upstream;\r\n* push result.\r\n\r\n## Architecture\r\n\r\n* canonical account model;\r\n* profile relationship;\r\n* guest strategy;\r\n* role model;\r\n* email model;\r\n* credential model;\r\n* session model;\r\n* reset model;\r\n* security-event model;\r\n* actor-reference strategy;\r\n* legacy compatibility strategy.\r\n\r\n## Migration totals\r\n\r\n* Player profiles examined;\r\n* Game Master users examined;\r\n* canonical accounts created;\r\n* profiles attached;\r\n* profiles created;\r\n* credentials migrated;\r\n* sessions migrated;\r\n* roles migrated;\r\n* actor fields backfilled;\r\n* explicit merges;\r\n* unresolved candidates;\r\n* skipped records;\r\n* failed records.\r\n\r\n## Implementation totals\r\n\r\n* files added;\r\n* files modified;\r\n* routes added;\r\n* routes adapted;\r\n* pages added;\r\n* services added;\r\n* schema models added;\r\n* fields added;\r\n* compatibility adapters retained.\r\n\r\n## Test totals\r\n\r\n* unit tests;\r\n* integration tests;\r\n* migration tests;\r\n* authorization tests;\r\n* privacy tests;\r\n* E2E tests;\r\n* passed;\r\n* failed;\r\n* skipped;\r\n* blocked.\r\n\r\n## Required proof\r\n\r\nProvide evidence for:\r\n\r\n1. one account accessing Player, Captain, and Creator;\r\n2. email remaining private;\r\n3. password reset with generic request response;\r\n4. reset-token single use;\r\n5. session revocation;\r\n6. guest claim preserving membership;\r\n7. guest merge resolving membership collision;\r\n8. existing Player migration;\r\n9. existing Game Master migration;\r\n10. ambiguous identity not auto-merged;\r\n11. canonical Creator actor write;\r\n12. canonical Captain actor write;\r\n13. canonical database untouched;\r\n14. branch pushed without merge.\r\n\r\n## Remaining limitations\r\n\r\nExplicitly identify later-phase work, including:\r\n\r\n* gaming-platform linking;\r\n* full public profiles;\r\n* Chronicle Passport history;\r\n* detailed statistics;\r\n* per-person artifact records;\r\n* Creator and Captain analytics;\r\n* Community Harbor;\r\n* achievements;\r\n* follows and blocking;\r\n* passkeys;\r\n* full MFA;\r\n* account export and deletion;\r\n* removal of any retained legacy compatibility tables.\r\n\r\nDo not describe later-phase Chronicle, invitation, artifact, completion, creation, Captain action, and community contribution belongs to a persistent \r\nperson, while that person retains granular control over what becomes visible to others.\r\nWhat Project Wayfarer Must Deliver\r\n Easy account creation using email/password, supported external identity providers, or invitation-first guest entry.\r\n Verified email history, accurate timing, endings, favorite moments, memories, keepsakes, and crew records.\r\n Per-person artifact discovery, ownership, assembly, favorites, collection progress, and profile display cases.\r\n Per-person Captain and Creator records, statistics, invitations, publishing history, and analytics.\r\n Typed and versioned preferences for experience, accessibility, Chronicle discovery, social behavior, notifications, and \r\nprivacy.\r\n Community Harbor identity, attribution, reviews, follows, completion posts, remix lineage, and public creator pages.\r\n Statistics derived from authoritative records, with rebuildable cached aggregates rather than fragile manually \r\nincremented counters.\r\n Granular privacy controls by profile section and record, not one crude global public/private switch.\r\nProgram Outcomes\r\nOutcome Result\r\nIdentity continuity A guest invited to one Chronicle can later claim an account \r\nwithout losing history, artifacts, or crew relationships.\r\nRole continuity The same person can play, Captain, create, review, and publish \r\nwithout duplicate identities.\r\nHistorical truth Every completion, invitation, artifact, and 2026     Page 5\r\n1. Purpose, Authority, and Scope\r\n1.1 Purpose\r\nThis document governs the design and implementation of the platform’s person-level identity system. It replaces the idea \r\nof a minimal “Player account” with a unified identity architecture capable of supporting play, Captain control, creation, \r\nartifacts, statistics, memories, invitations, Community Harbor, moderation, and long-term account security.\r\n1.2 Authority\r\nProject Wayfarer is the canonical requirement source for identity and profile behavior. Later implementation prompts, \r\ndesign records, database migrations, frontend components, and API contracts must trace back to this document. Where \r\ncurrent code differs, the implementation program must reconcile the code toward this specification rather than quietly \r\nredefining the requirement around current limitations.\r\n1.3 In Scope\r\n Canonical account and profile identity.\r\n Guest profiles, invitation-first entry, and account claiming.\r\n Email verification, password reset, session revocation, and provider login.\r\n Public and private profile surfaces.\r\n Linked gaming and social platforms.\r\n Player preferences and privacy controls.\r\n Chronicle, artifact, crew, Captain, Creator, achievement, and Community history.\r\n Statistics, analytics, caches, and rebuild behavior.\r\n Identity-related moderation, blocking, reporting, and safety.\r\n Migration from current PlayerProfile and GameMasterUser structures.\r\n Testing, operations, observability, data export, and deletion.\r\n1.4 Out of Scope for Initial Delivery\r\n Unrestricted direct messaging between users.\r\n Global competitive leaderboards by default.\r\n Payment processing and creator marketplace payouts.\r\n Automatic scraping of gaming-platform friends or presence without explicit authorization.\r\n Publishing private crew or relationship information by default.\r\n Using private email addresses as visible profile identifiers.\r\n Replacing Chronicle-specific gameplay systems unrelated to identity except where required for per-person history.\r\n\\n--- PAGE 6 ---\\nPROJECT WAYFARER  |  Player Identity, Chronicle Passport, and Personal History\r\nGoverning Architecture and Product Requirements  |  Version 1.0  |  July 21, 2026     Page 6\r\n2. Product Vision and Terminology\r\n2.1 Product Vision\r\nA person should experience the platform as a persistent personal voyage history. Their identity should feel like a \r\nChronicle Passport: a private record of everything they have experienced and created, with a curated public profile that \r\nshows only what they intentionally share.\r\n2.2 User-Facing Names\r\nContext Recommended label\r\nInternal program Project Wayfarer\r\nPrivate personal hub Chronicle Passport\r\nPublic identity page Profile\r\nChronicle participation record Voyage Record\r\nMemory collection Chronicle Memories\r\nPer-person artifact collection Artifact Cabinet or Relic Collection\r\nCaptain history Captain Log\r\nCreator work Creator Portfolio\r\nCommunity identity Community Harbor Profile\r\n2.3 Core Terms\r\nTerm Definition\r\nAccount Private security and authentication identity for one real person.\r\nProfile Person-facing identity, preferences, history, statistics, and public \r\npresentation.\r\nHandle Optional globally unique public identifier, such as @Kgray44.\r\nDisplay name Visible name chosen by the person; it need not be globally \r\nunique.\r\nClaimed profile A profile secured by a verified login method.\r\nGuest profile A limited profile created from an invitation or temporary entry \r\nbefore account claiming.\r\nChronicle A published reusable Tall Tale experience.\r\nVoyage A concrete playthrough of a version-pinned Chronicle.\r\nMembership A person’s relationship to a Voyage, including role, status, join, \r\nand completion.\r\nArtifact record A per-person record of discovery, custody, collection, assembly, \r\nfavorite status, and display.\r\nCommunity contribution A Chronicle, artifact, template, map, review, completion post, \r\nremix, translation, comment, or collection attributed to a person.\r\n\\n--- PAGE 7 ---\\nPROJECT WAYFARER  |  Player Identity, Chronicle Passport, and Personal History\r\nGoverning Architecture and Product Requirements  |  Version 1.0  |  July 21, 2026     Page 7\r\n3. Current Repository Baseline and Gap Analysis\r\n3.1 Existing Foundation\r\nThe current repository already contains a meaningful identity foundation. The present PlayerProfile supports an optional \r\nusername, optional password hash, display name, status, generic preferences, claimed timestamp, identity sessions, \r\nChronicle memberships, and invitations. The membership system records role, crew role, status, join and completion \r\ntimestamps, and personal library states such as pinned or hidden. Invitations can target a specific PlayerProfile.\r\nExisting capability Value to Wayfarer\r\nPlayerProfile with optional credentials Supports guest or unclaimed profiles that may later be secured.\r\ndisplayName Already separates visible identity from login credentials.\r\nclaimedAt Provides a direct migration path for invitation-first account \r\nclaiming.\r\nPlayerIdentitySession Provides a basis for persistent sessions and future device \r\nmanagement.\r\nPlaythroughMembership Provides the person-to-Voyage relationship required for \r\nindividual history.\r\nInvitation.intendedPlayerId Allows invitations and resulting Voyage history to target the \r\ncorrect person.\r\nInvitationEvent Provides authoritative invitation lifecycle facts.\r\nPublishedTaleVersion Allows each person’s history to remain tied to the exact \r\nimmutable Chronicle version played.\r\n3.2 Current Structural Gaps\r\n Split identities. PlayerProfile and GameMasterUser represent separate account systems. A person who plays, \r\nCaptains, and creates can become multiple unrelated identities.\r\n Raw actor identifiers. Tall Tale creators, session Captains, invitation creators, and some audit actors are stored as \r\ngeneric strings rather than governed relations to one canonical person.\r\n No verified contact identity. The current PlayerProfile does not provide verified email, recovery state, password-reset \r\ntokens, provider identities, or contact preferences.\r\n Generic preference blob. Preferences are stored as generic JSON without a formal typed, versioned, and queryable \r\ncontract.\r\n Session-level inventory. The current Tale Session inventory is shared at the Voyage level and cannot fully represent \r\nindividual discovery, custody, favorite status, profile display, or personal artifact notes.\r\n Limited personal history. Memberships identify participation, but do not yet provide complete per-person endings, \r\ntiming, choices, favorites, memories, artifact grants, reflections, or keepsakes.\r\n No Community identity layer. There is no complete public creator/player profile, follow graph, review attribution, \r\ncommunity contribution history, or visibility model.\r\n No recovery lifecycle. Forgotten-password flows, verified email, provider login, device management, and sign-out-\r\neverywhere behavior are not yet complete.\r\n3.3 Governing Reconciliation Decision\r\nDecision\r\nThe current PlayerProfile must evolve into the person-facing profile, while a canonical UserAccount becomes the private \r\nauthentication identity. GameMasterUser functionality must migrate into account role assignments and capabilities. One \r\nperson must not retain parallel Player and Game Master identities after migration.\r\n\\n--- PAGE 8 ---\\nPROJECT WAYFARER  |  Player Identity, Chronicle Passport, and Personal History\r\nGoverning Architecture and Product Requirements  |  Version 1.0  |  July 21, 2026     Page 8\r\n4. Governing Principles and Non-Negotiable Invariants\r\nPrinciple Requirement\r\nOne person, one account, one profile. Roles and capabilities may vary, but the underlying person \r\nidentity remains canonical.\r\nVisible identity is not login identity. Email, provider IDs, security state, reset tokens, and private \r\ncontact data are never exposed as profile identity.\r\nGuest entry must not destroy magic. Players can begin from an invitation without a heavy registration \r\nceremony, then claim and preserve their history later.\r\nHistory is version-pinned. Every Voyage record references the exact published Chronicle \r\nversion played.\r\nFacts are authoritative; counters are derived. Completions, invitations, artifacts, and publications live in source \r\nrecords. Summary statistics are rebuildable projections.\r\nPrivacy is granular. Each profile section and sensitive record can have its own \r\nvisibility, with safe defaults.\r\nShared and individual state are distinct. Crew inventory and personal artifact ownership may coexist but \r\nare never treated as identical.\r\nConsent controls provider integration. Linking Xbox, Steam, Discord, or another provider does not \r\nautomatically make the provider visible or grant all available \r\npermissions.\r\nSecurity changes revoke risk. Password resets, provider compromise, and explicit sign-out-\r\neverywhere actions invalidate affected sessions.\r\nDeletion does not falsify history. Public attribution and audit history use safe tombstones or actor \r\nsnapshots where legally and operationally necessary, while \r\nprivate personal data is removed or anonymized according to \r\npolicy.\r\nCommunity publication is sanitized. Live Voyage data, private memories, crew details, and \r\nunpublished content never become public merely because a \r\nrelated Chronicle or artifact is shared.\r\nAccessibility is personal and portable. Experience preferences follow the person across Chronicles and \r\ndevices while allowing Chronicle-specific temporary overrides.\r\n\\n--- PAGE 9 ---\\nPROJECT WAYFARER  |  Player Identity, Chronicle Passport, and Personal History\r\nGoverning Architecture and Product Requirements  |  Version 1.0  |  July 21, 2026     Page 9\r\n5. Canonical Identity Architecture\r\n5.1 High-Level Model\r\nThe platform SHALL separate private security identity from public and personal profile identity. A canonical account owns \r\nexactly one Player profile. Role assignments grant capabilities to the same account.\r\nUserAccount\r\n  - verified login identities\r\n  - password credentials and recovery\r\n  - linked providers and sessions\r\n  - account status and security events\r\nPlayerProfile\r\n  - display name, handle, avatar, banner, biography\r\n  - preferences and privacy\r\n  - Chronicle Passport and artifacts\r\n  - Captain, Creator, achievement, and Community history\r\nRoleAssignment\r\n  - PLAYER, CAPTAIN, CREATOR, MODERATOR, ADMINISTRATOR\r\n5.2 Account and Profile Cardinality\r\n One UserAccount MUST own exactly one active PlayerProfile.\r\n A PlayerProfile MAY begin as an unclaimed guest profile without a UserAccount, but it MUST have a controlled claiming \r\npath.\r\n One UserAccount MAY hold multiple role assignments.\r\n A role assignment MUST NOT create a second person identity.\r\n Merging duplicate profiles MUST be an explicit, audited operation with conflict handling.\r\n Provider identities MUST map to one UserAccount unless an administrative recovery or merge process resolves a \r\nconflict.\r\n5.3 Role and Capability Model\r\nRole Core capabilities\r\nPLAYER Accept invitations, participate in Voyages, maintain Chronicle \r\nPassport, artifacts, memories, preferences, and Community \r\nactivity.\r\nCAPTAIN Create and manage Voyage sessions, send invitations, control \r\nprogression, release hints, perform guarded recovery, and \r\nreview Captain analytics.\r\nCREATOR Create, publish, maintain, import, export, and share Chronicles, \r\nartifacts, templates, and other reusable content.\r\nMODERATOR Review reports, quarantine content, apply sanc…24 tokens truncated…ecorded per person while \r\nremaining distinct from crew inventory.\r\nPreferences Experience, accessibility, Chronicle, social, notification, and privacy \r\npreferences are typed, versioned, and validated.\r\nStatistics Profile statistics reconcile with authoritative records and can be \r\nrebuilt from source facts.\r\nCaptain and Creator Captain and Creator activity is attributed to the same person identity \r\nand has private/public visibility separation.\r\nCommunity Community contributions, completion posts, reviews, and remixes \r\nhave persistent attribution and respect blocks and privacy.\r\nDeletion and export Users can export personal data and complete a governed deletion \r\nflow without corrupting other people’s historical records.\r\nSecurity Sessions, reset tokens, provider links, and sensitive actions follow \r\nleast-privilege, reauthentication, rate limiting, and audit rules.\r\nAccessibility Profile and settings experiences are keyboard accessible, screen-\r\nreader compatible, and respect persistent accessibility preferences.\r\n\\n--- PAGE 37 ---\\nPROJECT WAYFARER  |  Player Identity, Chronicle Passport, and Personal History\r\nGoverning Architecture and Product Requirements  |  Version 1.0  |  July 21, 2026     Page 37\r\n33. Test Strategy\r\n33.1 Unit Tests\r\n Preference schema validation and migration.\r\n Visibility resolution for every section and viewer relationship.\r\n Metric calculation and versioning.\r\n Password reset token creation, validation, expiration, and single use.\r\n Provider identity mapping and rename handling.\r\n Artifact recipient policies and assembly state.\r\n Achievement eligibility.\r\n Account deletion/anonymization decisions.\r\n33.2 Integration Tests\r\n Register, verify email, login, refresh, logout, and sign out everywhere.\r\n Invitation-first guest creation and later claiming.\r\n Merge guest history into an authenticated existing account.\r\n Link and unlink providers with token redaction.\r\n Create per-person Chronicle record from Voyage completion.\r\n Create per-person artifact records from grants.\r\n Rebuild profile statistics from authoritative records.\r\n Migrate GameMasterUser and PlayerProfile into one identity.\r\n Export and deletion flows.\r\n33.3 Authorization and Privacy Matrix\r\nTests must cover the profile owner, shared crew member, follower, registered stranger, blocked user, unauthenticated \r\nvisitor, Captain, Creator collaborator, Moderator, Administrator, and support operator. For each viewer, test every profile \r\nsection, invitation record, memory, artifact, provider identity, and statistic visibility.\r\n33.4 Browser and Accessibility Tests\r\n Desktop and mobile profile navigation.\r\n Keyboard-only operation.\r\n Screen reader labels and announcements.\r\n Text zoom and responsive reflow.\r\n Reduced motion and high contrast.\r\n Public-profile preview and privacy editing.\r\n Avatar, banner, and media upload accessibility.\r\n 3D artifact accessible fallback.\r\n33.5 Security Tests\r\n Account enumeration.\r\n Credential stuffing and rate limiting.\r\n Reset-token replay.\r\n Session fixation and revocation.\r\n OAuth state, nonce, and account-link confusion.\r\n Cross-account IDOR.\r\n Blocked-user recommendation and invitation bypass.\r\n Private field leakage in public APIs, logs, errors, caches, and analytics.\r\n Deletion and export authorization.\r\n33.6 Migration Tests\r\n Deterministic isolated database fixtures.\r\n Before/after reconciliation counts.\r\n Duplicate identity mapping scenarios.\r\n Partial failure and restart.\r\n Rollback or restore rehearsal.\r\n No mutation of canonical production data during test runs.\r\n\\n--- PAGE 38 ---\\nPROJECT WAYFARER  |  Player Identity, Chronicle Passport, and Personal History\r\nGoverning Architecture and Product Requirements  |  Version 1.0  |  July 21, 2026     Page 38\r\n34. Operations, Observability, and Support\r\n34.1 Operational Metrics\r\n Registration and verification success.\r\n Password reset request and completion rates.\r\n Provider link errors.\r\n Guest claim and merge conflicts.\r\n Session revocation and suspicious login events.\r\n Profile projection errors.\r\n Statistics rebuild lag and mismatches.\r\n Notification delivery failures.\r\n Data export and deletion job status.\r\n34.2 Support Console\r\n Search account by safe internal identifiers or verified contact under authorization.\r\n Inspect sanitized account state and role assignments.\r\n View session and security-event summaries.\r\n Resend verification or reset communication without exposing token.\r\n Start guarded profile merge or recovery workflow.\r\n Rebuild statistics and projections.\r\n Inspect invitation and membership relationships.\r\n Export audit timeline.\r\n Apply restrictions or moderation actions with reason and correlation ID.\r\n34.3 No Direct Database Repair\r\nRoutine support should not directly edit profile counters, role strings, invitation statuses, or artifact ownership in the \r\ndatabase. Repairs must use governed services or commands that validate invariants and create audit records.\r\n34.4 Backups and Recovery\r\n Account, profile, membership, artifact, memory, and attribution data are included in backup scope.\r\n Provider access tokens and secrets follow encrypted backup policy or are excluded where reauthorization is safer.\r\n Restore procedures verify foreign-key integrity and statistics rebuild.\r\n A restored environment must invalidate or carefully revalidate active security sessions according to incident policy.\r\n\\n--- PAGE 39 ---\\nPROJECT WAYFARER  |  Player Identity, Chronicle Passport, and Personal History\r\nGoverning Architecture and Product Requirements  |  Version 1.0  |  July 21, 2026     Page 39\r\n35. Explicit Non-Goals\r\n Using email addresses as public display names.\r\n Creating separate accounts for Player, Captain, Creator, and Community roles.\r\n Treating generic preferences JSON as the complete preference architecture.\r\n Treating session-level inventory as per-person artifact ownership.\r\n Publishing exact invitation recipients or private relationship history by default.\r\n Guessing favorite moments solely from time spent on a screen.\r\n Maintaining unrebuildable profile counters as the only source of truth.\r\n Launching unrestricted direct messaging in the initial program.\r\n Building a global popularity score or mandatory competitive leaderboard.\r\n Automatically linking or displaying gaming platforms without explicit consent.\r\n Allowing account deletion to rewrite or corrupt other people’s valid historical records.\r\n Exposing live Voyage state through Community profile endpoints.\r\n\\n--- PAGE 40 ---\\nPROJECT WAYFARER  |  Player Identity, Chronicle Passport, and Personal History\r\nGoverning Architecture and Product Requirements  |  Version 1.0  |  July 21, 2026     Page 40\r\n36. Decision Register and Future Extensions\r\nDecision Status Notes\r\nOne account and profile per person Accepted governing requirement Roles are capabilities.\r\nGuest invitation entry before registration Accepted History must survive claiming.\r\nDisplay name separate from email Accepted Handle optional and unique.\r\nProvider-neutral external identity layer Accepted Discord, Steam, Xbox prioritized subject to \r\nAPI feasibility.\r\nGranular visibility by section Accepted Safe defaults required.\r\nPer-person artifact ledger Accepted Separate from crew inventory.\r\nStatistics derived from authoritative facts Accepted Cached aggregates rebuildable.\r\nDirect messaging Deferred Requires mature moderation and safety.\r\nGlobal leaderboards Not default Optional Chronicle-specific feature only.\r\nMarketplace and payments Deferred Community sharing precedes commerce.\r\nPasskeys and MFA Planned advanced phase Privileged roles may require earlier MFA.\r\nFriends versus follows terminology Open product decision Initial architecture should support follows \r\nand crew relationships without requiring \r\nreciprocal friendship.\r\nHandle rename frequency Open policy decision Must support redirects and impersonation \r\nprotection.\r\nMinor accounts Open legal/product decision Requires jurisdiction-specific safety design.\r\n\\n--- PAGE 41 ---\\nPROJECT WAYFARER  |  Player Identity, Chronicle Passport, and Personal History\r\nGoverning Architecture and Product Requirements  |  Version 1.0  |  July 21, 2026     Page 41\r\nAppendix A. Metric Catalog\r\nMetric Definition Default visibility\r\nChronicles invited Count of valid invitation records addressed to \r\nthe person.\r\nPrivate; optional aggregate public.\r\nChronicles accepted Accepted invitation or direct membership count. Private by default.\r\nChronicles completed Distinct completed Voyage memberships. Optional public aggregate.\r\nActive Chronicles Current active memberships. Private.\r\nCompletion rate Completed eligible Voyages divided by eligible \r\nstarted Voyages under formula version.\r\nPrivate; Creator/Captain aggregate only with \r\ncontext.\r\nTotal active time Sum of active-duration metric across eligible \r\nVoyages.\r\nPrivate by default.\r\nAverage completion time Mean or median under documented metric \r\nversion.\r\nPrivate; optional per-Chronicle.\r\nArtifacts discovered Distinct personal artifact records in discovery or \r\nownership states.\r\nOptional public aggregate.\r\nCollections completed Completed assembly or collection definitions. Optional public.\r\nUnique crew members Distinct profiles sharing eligible Voyages. Private aggregate unless shared.\r\nInvitations sent Invitation records created by the person as \r\nCaptain.\r\nPrivate; optional public aggregate.\r\nPlayers hosted Distinct accepted memberships in Captained \r\nVoyages.\r\nOptional public aggregate.\r\nChronicles created Distinct Tall Tales owned by the Creator. Public/private by publication state.\r\nPublished Chronicles Current or historical public/unlisted published \r\nworks.\r\nPublic portfolio.\r\nCommunity installs Valid package installs of public content. Public aggregate.\r\nReviews posted Public reviews authored by the person. Public activity unless deleted/hidden.\r\nRemixes Public derivative works with lineage. Public portfolio.\r\n\\n--- PAGE 44 ---\\nPROJECT WAYFARER  |  Player Identity, Chronicle Passport, and Personal History\r\nGoverning Architecture and Product Requirements  |  Version 1.0  |  July 21, 2026     Page 44\r\nAppendix C. Recommended Privacy Defaults\r\nProfile element Recommended default\r\nDisplay name REGISTERED_USERS or PUBLIC based on account mode\r\nHandle PUBLIC when reserved\r\nAvatar and banner Same as profile visibility\r\nEmail and security ONLY_ME\r\nLinked providers ONLY_ME\r\nChronicle completion count ONLY_ME\r\nDetailed Voyage history ONLY_ME\r\nCompletion times ONLY_ME\r\nArtifact collection ONLY_ME\r\nSelected artifact display case PUBLIC only after explicit selection\r\nCrew relationships CREW_ONLY\r\nInvitations and recipients ONLY_ME\r\nMemories and photos ONLY_ME\r\nCreator public portfolio PUBLIC for published items\r\nCaptain detailed statistics ONLY_ME\r\nCaptain aggregate statistics ONLY_ME until explicitly shared\r\nAchievements ONLY_ME; selected badges may be PUBLIC\r\nCommunity reviews and posts PUBLIC when intentionally posted\r\nSearch discoverability REGISTERED_USERS by default; user configurable\r\n\\n--- PAGE 45 ---\\nPROJECT WAYFARER  |  Player Identity, Chronicle Passport, and Personal History\r\nGoverning Architecture and Product Requirements  |  Version 1.0  |  July 21, 2026     Page 45\r\nAppendix D. Canonical User Journeys\r\nD.1 Sera Accepts an Invitation Without an Account\r\n1.  Sera opens the private invitation.\r\n2.  The platform validates the invitation and asks for her visible name.\r\n3.  An unclaimed profile is created and tied to the membership.\r\n4.  She begins the Voyage immediately.\r\n5.  Artifacts and completion progress attach to that profile.\r\n6.  Afterward, she claims it using verified email or a linked provider.\r\n7.  Her completed Voyage, artifacts, memories, crew relationship, and invitation history remain intact.\r\nD.2 KG Plays, Captains, and Creates\r\n1.  KG signs into one account.\r\n2.  The account owns one profile.\r\n3.  Role assignments grant Player, Captain, and Creator capabilities.\r\n4.  KG completes a Chronicle as a Player.\r\n5.  KG Captains a private Voyage for Sera.\r\n6.  KG publishes an artifact pack to Community Harbor.\r\n7.  All activity appears under the same profile with separate public and private visibility.\r\nD.3 Forgotten Password\r\n1.  User requests reset with email.\r\n2.  The platform returns a generic confirmation.\r\n3.  A single-use link is delivered to the verified email.\r\n4.  The user chooses a new password.\r\n5.  The token is consumed and older sessions are revoked.\r\n6.  The user receives a security confirmation and may review active devices.\r\nD.4 Linking Discord but Keeping It Private\r\n1.  User links Discord using approved OAuth scopes.\r\n2.  Discord becomes an available login method.\r\n3.  The user leaves profile visibility set to ONLY_ME.\r\n4.  Community visitors do not see the Discord identity.\r\n5.  The user may later enable invitation delivery or public display independently.\r\nD.5 Per-Person Artifact Award\r\n1.  The crew reveals a compass fragment.\r\n2.  The Chronicle block declares “grant to all active Players.”\r\n3.  Each active profile receives a PlayerArtifactRecord.\r\n4.  The crew inventory also receives the shared fragment.\r\n5.  KG marks it as a favorite; Sera adds a private memory.\r\n6.  Both personal records remain independent while referencing the same reveal event.\r\nD.6 Public Completion Post\r\n1.  Player completes a private Chronicle.\r\n2.  The private Voyage record is created automatically.\r\n3.  The Player selects approved cover, completion badge, one photo, and spoiler-free reaction.\r\n4.  The platform creates a separate public completion post.\r\n5.  Crew names appear only when each involved person permits it.\r\n6.  Deleting the post does not delete the private completion history.\r\n\\n--- PAGE 46 ---\\nPROJECT WAYFARER  |  Player Identity, Chronicle Passport, and Personal History\r\nGoverning Architecture and Product Requirements  |  Version 1.0  |  July 21, 2026     Page 46\r\nAppendix E. It is the identity backbone for Chronicles, artifacts, Captain control, Creator \r\nwork, and Community Harbor.\r\nImplementations must preserve the full intent of this document. A technically functioning login screen does not satisfy \r\nProject Wayfarer unless the person-level history, privacy, recovery, attribution, and per-person records defined here are \r\ncomplete.\r\nEND OF GOVERNING DOCUMENT\r\n", "type": "input_text"}]

It follows `Project_Wayfarer_Player_Identity_Governing_Document.pdf` (v1.0, 2026-07-21) and the Phase 1 implementation brief. It deliberately does not begin provider linking, public profiles, Chronicle Passport projections, artifact ownership, analytics, Community Harbor, passkeys, MFA, export, deletion, or legacy Campaign redesign.\n+\n+## Preflight (2026-07-21)\n+\n+| Item | Recorded value |\n+| --- | --- |\n+| Repository root | `\\\\\\\\US-VT-FS01\\\\Users\\\\kgray\\\\My Documents\\\\treasurehunt\\\\forever-treasure-companion` |\n+| Canonical checkout | `\\\\\\\\US-VT-FS01\\\\Users\\\\kgray\\\\My Documents\\\\treasurehunt\\\\forever-treasure-companion` |\n+| Phase 1 worktree | `\\\\\\\\US-VT-FS01\\\\Users\\\\kgray\\\\My Documents\\\\treasurehunt\\\\Forever-Treasure-Wayfarer-Phase-1` |\n+| Branch | `codex/project-wayfarer-phase1-unified-identity` |\n+| Base and fetched `origin/main` | `0ecd2f9cca6116e2f7f9ab4408ade749fb061e72` |\n+| Worktree start state | Clean; no staged, unstaged, or untracked files |\n+| Canonical checkout state | `work/lanternwake-latest`, behind its upstream by seven commits, with three owner-provided untracked governing PDFs; untouched by this work |\n+| Active visible worktrees | canonical Lanternwake, Phase 3 command center, Integration, Universal Language, Lanternwake Phase 5, Phase 4 acceptance, and a detached local Phase 5 validation worktree |\n+| Visible Wayfarer/identity branches | none before this branch |\n+\n+`git fetch origin --prune --no-tags` completed before worktree creation. The worktree was created directly from the recorded remote commit. The initial checkout on the UNC share exceeded the normal command window but completed cleanly; no partially-created directory was reused.\n+\n+High-conflict baseline files were inspected before implementation: `prisma/schema.prisma`, `src/platform/auth.ts`, `src/platform/invitations.ts`, `src/platform/libraries.ts`, `src/platform/policy.ts`, Tall Tale authoring/progression services, Captain routes, and Player invitation routes. The base commit contains integrated Lanternwake and Universal Language work; Phase 1 preserves those surfaces rather than restoring older code.\n+\n+## Frozen architecture\n+\n+### Canonical person model\n+\n+`UserAccount` is the private, canonical identity. It has exactly one `PlayerProfile` once claimed and may have multiple active `AccountRoleAssignment` records. A guest is represented by a canonical account with `GUEST_UNCLAIMED` status from the moment invitation acceptance creates a profile. This preferred strategy keeps account and profile IDs stable through claiming, permits canonical guest sessions, and makes guest claiming idempotent.\n+\n+`PlayerProfile.id` remains stable. `PlayerProfile.accountId` is nullable and unique only as an additive compatibility measure; claimed accounts always have one profile, while a historic unclaimed profile is attached in the migration or invitation flow. A database uniqueness constraint prevents a profile from being attached twice; services enforce the reciprocal one-profile account invariant.\n+\n+### Login, display, email, and credentials\n+\n+* `displayName` remains the visible person label, is required for registration and guest entry, is not globally unique, and never defaults to an email address.\n+* Existing `PlayerProfile.username` is a **legacy private login alias**. It remains usable during the compatibility window but is not newly written by registration and is never exposed as a public handle.\n+* `AccountEmail` owns a unique lowercase/trimmed `normalizedEmail`, a retained display form, primary and verification state. No email field is included in Player, Captain, or Creator public responses.\n+* `AccountCredential` is the sole canonical password owner. Existing bcrypt hashes are copied without rehashing; the successful login path may upgrade a legacy hash only with supplied plaintext. New passwords require at least 12 characters and a non-whitespace mix, are bcrypt-hashed, and never logged.\n+* Email verification and password-reset selectors are random 32-byte URL-safe values. Persistent storage contains only SHA-256 hashes, an expiry, consumption time, and metadata safe for audit. The raw token exists only in the transient transactional-email boundary and test outbox.\n+\n+### Sessions, CSRF, and security\n+\n+`AccountSession` replaces person authentication use of `PlayerIdentitySession` and `GameMasterSession`. It stores a hashed opaque token, independent CSRF secret, expiry, last-seen, revocation, and a privacy-safe device label derived from the user agent. Login and password reset rotate/revoke as appropriate. State-changing cookie routes require the session CSRF value; authentication bootstrap endpoints are same-origin JSON endpoints and use strict cookies. Session listings omit token and IP data. Locked and suspended accounts cannot authenticate or use role protections.\n+\n+`SecurityEvent` records account lifecycle, registration, verification, reset request/consumption, sign-in success/failure, claiming, merge, and session revocation. It never stores raw credential, reset, verification, or session values.\n+\n+### Roles and legacy Game Master transition\n+\n+`AccountRoleAssignment` belongs to `UserAccount`, with the global governed roles `PLAYER`, `CAPTAIN`, `CREATOR`, `MODERATOR`, and `ADMINISTRATOR`. Authorization resolves roles from the authenticated canonical account, never from display names, email, or raw legacy strings. `GameMasterUser`, `GameMasterSession`, and `PlatformRoleAssignment` remain read-compatible only for phased data migration. New Game Master identities are forbidden.\n+\n+Every existing `GameMasterUser` receives a canonical account/profile and receives equivalent roles. A deterministic candidate with a matching legacy Player username is not automatically merged: it is recorded as an unresolved duplicate candidate unless an explicit migration map proves ownership. This protects distinct people who happen to share a name.\n+\n+### Guest claiming and collision policy\n+\n+Invitation acceptance creates or attaches a persistent guest account/profile and guest account session. Claiming into a new account adds email and credential in place, verifies the email, converts status to `PENDING_VERIFICATION` then `ACTIVE`, and preserves memberships, invitations, and events.\n+\n+Claiming into an existing authenticated account is an explicit merge. It moves guest membership/invitation ownership only where the target has no membership for that Voyage. If both profiles have a membership for the same Voyage, the canonical target membership wins and missing timestamps/states are deterministically combined; no duplicate membership is created. The guest account is marked merged, guest sessions are revoked, and both the merge and collision decision are audited. Repeated requests return the same resolved target without duplicating records.\n+\n+### Canonical actor cutover\n+\n+New Tall Tale, draft, published version, asset, Tale Session Captain, invitation, invitation-event, reveal, platform-audit, and Tale Session event writes receive optional canonical `actorAccountId` relations. Existing raw IDs remain immutable historical snapshots and compatibility lookups; they are no longer authorization sources for new code. Actor display snapshots are stored as existing labels or explicit metadata rather than resolved from private email.\n+\n+Legacy Campaign `ProgressEvent.actor`, `PreparedAction.preparedBy`, and `AdminAuditLog.userId` are inventoried but deliberately not broadly migrated in Phase 1; compatible canonical actor seams are added only where current services write them.\n+\n+### Transactional email boundary and later seams\n+\n+Email delivery is a narrow interface with a development/test outbox. Failed delivery does not roll back a correctly-created reset request; it is recorded as a delivery failure for retry/operations. Provider integration receives an account-owned identity seam but no unsupported provider UI or provider connection is added. Typed preferences, public-profile visibility, Chronicle history/statistics, artifacts, and deletion/export retain their current data without being represented as a generic new profile blob.\n+\n+## Actor-field inventory and disposition\n+\n+| Existing field | Current source | Phase 1 disposition |\n+| --- | --- | --- |\n+| `TallTale.creatorId` | Game Master string | add `creatorAccountId`; new studio writes use it |\n+| `TaleDraft.createdBy`, `PublishedTaleVersion.publishedBy`, `TaleAsset.createdBy` | Game Master string | add canonical account relations; retain snapshot strings |\n+| `TaleSession.captainId` | Game Master string | add `captainAccountId`; new Captain/preview writes use it |\n+| `Invitation.createdBy` | Captain string | add `creatorAccountId`; new invitation writes use it |\n+| `InvitationEvent.actorId`, `PlatformAuditEvent.actorId`, `RevealState.revealedBy`, `TaleSessionEvent.sourceId` | mixed raw actor strings | add canonical account relation where actor is authenticated; retain historical raw value/type |\n+| `GameMasterSession.userId`, `PlatformRoleAssignment.accountId`, `AdminAuditLog.userId` | Game Master relation | migrate/mirror into canonical sessions, roles, and audit actor seam |\n+| `PreparedAction.preparedBy`, `ProgressEvent.actor` | legacy Campaign strings | compatibility-only inventory; no broad Campaign migration in Phase 1 |\n+\n+## Migration, reconciliation, and restore\n+\n+The migration is additive and idempotent. It first creates canonical tables and nullable relations, then runs a transaction-safe backfill in bounded batches. Player profiles receive accounts according to claimed/credential status; unclaimed profiles get guest accounts. Game Master records receive canonical accounts and profiles. Exact identifiers are not merged merely because names match. A `WayfarerMigrationRecord` stores source, target, status, and diagnostic reason, allowing resume without duplicate account or role creation.\n+\n+The rehearsal runs only against the repository validation database created by the existing isolation harness. It reports examined profiles and Game Masters; created/attached profiles/accounts; credentials, sessions, roles, and actor fields migrated; explicit merges; unresolved candidates; skipped and failed records. Reconciliation compares source memberships, invitations, invitation events, Creator ownership, Captain ownership, and eligible sessions before and after. Production migration requires a verified backup and a successful isolated rehearsal. Rollback is restore-from-backup plus removal of the additive migration only after no application deployment points at it; no destructive in-place rollback is proposed.\n+\n+## Compatibility boundaries\n+\n+Player sign-in, invitation acceptance, Captain guards, Creator Studio guards, session-cookie reads, and role policy are adapted to canonical services. During transition they can resolve legacy cookie/session rows to a canonical account, rotate into a canonical session, and preserve existing response shapes. Existing Player, Captain, Creator, invitation, publishing, language, and animation experiences are not redesigned. All private identity data is excluded from existing library and player serializers.\n+\n+## Test and database isolation contract\n+\n+Focused tests cover registration, email verification, password recovery, sessions, guest claim/merge, legacy migration, canonical role authorization, actor writes, CSRF, token redaction, and private-response shaping. Migration fixtures assert deterministic counts and ambiguous-name non-merging. The repository validation harness creates an isolated SQLite database, records its identity, and verifies the canonical development database was not mutated. The final gate is the repository-supported `scripts/test-all.ps1` command, run once after focused tests are green; this record and the validation record distinguish task failures from inherited blockers.\n+\n+## Phase 2 seams (not implemented)\n+\n+External gaming/social provider connection, account passkeys/MFA, public profile rendering, Chronicle Passport/history projections, typed preference migration, per-person artifact records, derived statistics, Community Harbor, follows/blocks UI, achievement systems, analytics, export, deletion, and legacy table removal remain later phases.\n*** End Patch";

\"\" : new URLSearchParams(window.location.search).get(\"token\") ?? \"\";\n+\n+  async function submit(event: FormEvent<HTMLFormElement>) {\n+    event.preventDefault(); setBusy(true); setError(\"\"); setMessage(\"\");\n+    const data = Object.fromEntries(new FormData(event.currentTarget));\n+    if (mode === \"register\" && data.password !== data.confirmPassword) { setError(\"Passwords do not match.\"); setBusy(false); return; }\n+    try {\n+      const response = await fetch(endpoints[mode as Exclude<Mode, \"security\">], { method: \"POST\", headers: { \"content-type\": \"application/json\", ...(csrf ? { \"x-csrf-token\": csrf } : {}) }, body: JSON.stringify({ ...data, ...(mode === \"merge\" ? { confirm: true } : {}) }) });\n+      const body = await response.json();\n+      if (!response.ok) throw new Error(body.error ??
